  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_78019b64-beb6-4178-bc04-9af0e2893efa'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">It's highly likely that Henry Sugar is the same person as Oswald from My Uncle Oswald, as they both have the same motto "it is better to incur a mild <a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">It's highly likely that Henry Sugar is the same person as Oswald from My Uncle Oswald, as they both have the same motto "it is better to incur a mild rebuke than perform an onerous chore," or something along the lines. <a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_2278144239" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2278144239" />
    <a title="Miranda Reads" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/71848701-miranda-reads"><img alt="Miranda Reads" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1592243041p2/71848701.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2278144239?book_show_action=true">Jan 30, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Miranda Reads" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Miranda Reads" href="/user/show/71848701-miranda-reads">Miranda Reads</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/71848701-miranda-reads?shelf=2018-finer-books-club-reading-chall">2018-finer-books-club-reading-chall</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2278144239" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer467171196894550554"><b>A (somewhat) delightful variety of short stories. </b><br/><br/>After reading <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/44516.Switch_Bitch' title='Switch Bitch by Roald Dahl' rel='nofollow noopener'>Switch Bitch</a> (also a short story collection by Dahl), I did not have much hope for this collection. If you have not read those stories, I could sum them up on three words: Pervy, Misogynistic and Disturbing. While this one was certainly better, this is definitely not one of my favorites.<br/><br/><b>The Boy Who Talked to Animals</b> - An enormous sea turtle becomes caught by fishermen - who themselves are caught between killing, eating and dismember</span>
  <span id="freeText467171196894550554" style="display:none"><b>A (somewhat) delightful variety of short stories. </b><br /><br />After reading <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/44516.Switch_Bitch" title="Switch Bitch by Roald Dahl" rel="nofollow noopener">Switch Bitch</a> (also a short story collection by Dahl), I did not have much hope for this collection. If you have not read those stories, I could sum them up on three words: Pervy, Misogynistic and Disturbing. While this one was certainly better, this is definitely not one of my favorites.<br /><br /><b>The Boy Who Talked to Animals</b> - An enormous sea turtle becomes caught by fishermen - who themselves are caught between killing, eating and dismembering the poor creature. A little boy can understand animals and begs them to let the beast go.<br /><br /><b>The Hitch-hiker</b> - Quirky Dahl at his best! A fancy-car driver picks up a hitchhiker and gets far more than he bargained for - this man has some very deft fingers and could steal the anything from anyone.<br /><br /><b>The Mildenhall Treasure</b> - bit of a disappointment. One man discovers a treasure but is swindled out of it. No comeuppance or revenge. <br /><br /><b>The Swan</b> - I disliked it from start to finish. Two bullies get ahold of a gun and threaten a wimpy kid into doing dangerous stunts for their amusements. These bullies were absolute monsters - culiminating in them dismembering a mother swan, tying her severed wings to the wimpy kid, forcing him to climb a tree and jump off (for him to "fly").<b>
  <u> Absolutely terrible.</u>
</b><br /><br /><b>The Wonderful Story of Henry Sugar</b> - This one was...surprisingly good. We start with a rich, snotty man who wants to learn the secrets of the yogis to win at casinos. We end with a well-rounded, sweet and generous man. Love the transition.<br /><br /><b> Lucky Break</b> - Dahl reflects on how he began writing. Includes several instances from his past (including events from Boy and Going Solo). Dahl uses his signature style to describe the terrible beatings he suffered and the crazy behavior he witnessed throughout his time at boarding school. While there were more good times than bad, I would not recommend such an experience.<br /><br /><b> A Piece of Cake</b> - Dahl's first-ever piece of writing (as mentioned in Lucky Break). I already read the longer version in Going Solo by Dahl so it was fun to connect the snippets to the longer story.<br /><br /><b>Audiobook Comments</b><br />Well-read. The voice did not inflect too much or vary in tone. Became a bit monotonous.<br /><br /><i>The Finer Books Club - 2018 Reading Challenge: A book of short stories</i><br /><br /><a href="http://bit.ly/33ii2CT" rel="nofollow noopener">YouTube</a> | <a href="http://www.mirandareads.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/miranda.reads/?hl=en" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/Miranda_Reads" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | Snapchat @miranda.reads <br /><br />Happy Reading!</span>
  <a data-text-id="467171196894550554" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2036111547" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2036111547" />

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2036111547?book_show_action=true">Apr 18, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Calista" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Calista" href="/user/show/16731747-calista">Calista</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780141304700" href="/book/show/385246.The_Wonderful_Story_of_Henry_Sugar_and_Six_More">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16731747-calista?shelf=1975-1979">1975-1979</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16731747-calista?shelf=bage-middle-grade">bage-middle-grade</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16731747-calista?shelf=genre-nonfiction">genre-nonfiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16731747-calista?shelf=bage-mature">bage-mature</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16731747-calista?shelf=z-roald-dahl">z-roald-dahl</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16731747-calista?shelf=histiorical">histiorical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16731747-calista?shelf=myth-folktale-fable">myth-folktale-fable</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16731747-calista?shelf=genre-fantasy">genre-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16731747-calista?shelf=classic">classic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16731747-calista?shelf=genre-memoir-biography">genre-memoir-biography</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2036111547" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5959611299242238121">The short story collection contains 7 stories:<br/>The Boy Who Talked with Animals 4 stars<br/>The Hitch-Hiker 3 stars<br/>The Mildenhall Treasure 3 stars<br/>The Swan 3 stars<br/>The Wonderful Story of Henry Sugar 4 stars<br/>Lucky Break 4 stars<br/>A Piece of Cake 2 stars<br/><br/>There are several of these that I really enjoyed and the rest were well done. I love Henry Sugar and the method Henry goes about getting 'powers' after reading about a yogi. Concentration is a powerful thing. That was a well done story and I enjoyed the way it </span>
  <span id="freeText5959611299242238121" style="display:none">The short story collection contains 7 stories:<br />The Boy Who Talked with Animals 4 stars<br />The Hitch-Hiker 3 stars<br />The Mildenhall Treasure 3 stars<br />The Swan 3 stars<br />The Wonderful Story of Henry Sugar 4 stars<br />Lucky Break 4 stars<br />A Piece of Cake 2 stars<br /><br />There are several of these that I really enjoyed and the rest were well done. I love Henry Sugar and the method Henry goes about getting 'powers' after reading about a yogi. Concentration is a powerful thing. That was a well done story and I enjoyed the way it started. A super story. <br /><br />I thought his auto-biographical piece on how Roald began his writing career was wondering and it tied into this autobiography as well with the fighter pilot. He basically walked right into his career. It was pre-ordained, pretty much. He has some great tips for writing as well and he goes into what his English Lit professor said about his writing, which made you realize they probably didn't know what they were talking about. They were just meanies. <br /><br />The last one I really enjoyed was the Boy who could talk with animals. I loved the compassion in this story and the boy riding around on a turtle. It has that magic twist a Roald DAhl story can spin. <br /><br />I think these 3 stories are the strongest. <br /><br />The Swan is a good story, but it was stressful. It's about bullying and it doesn't have a happy ending in my opinion. This is obviously how he felt at school as a boy being bullied. I was driving home in traffic and this story was not good for that as it was so stressful and hard to read. It is painful, just painful in all ways. It's about human cruelty. It's good, but I won't read it again. <br /><br />I thought the Hitchhiker and Mildenhall Treasure (which is non-fiction) were fun and cute. They didn't blow me away, but they rounded out the book nicely. <br /><br />The last: Piece of Cake was filler. It was ok, but it did not hook me<br /><br />I'm glad I was finally able to finish this up and I think that this finishes off all the books of Roald Dahl that are considered his children's books. I still need to read his adult works like Uncle Oswalt, but I'm mostly done with his stuff. It has been a pleasure. </span>
  <a data-text-id="5959611299242238121" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5464046-porshajo?shelf=challenge">challenge</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1815326351" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16772747805309963503">I picked this one up after seeing a review on GR and started it almost two months ago. It's a book of short stories and I would pick it up when I needed a quick break from work, current reading, chores, etc. So it taking me two months to read was not a sign of it being boring. All this and I probably had too many books going on at once.<br/><br/>This book contains stories that are quite different from some of the usual Dahl books. Some are pretty short and some are longer, with a total of seven stories. T</span>
  <span id="freeText16772747805309963503" style="display:none">I picked this one up after seeing a review on GR and started it almost two months ago. It's a book of short stories and I would pick it up when I needed a quick break from work, current reading, chores, etc. So it taking me two months to read was not a sign of it being boring. All this and I probably had too many books going on at once.<br /><br />This book contains stories that are quite different from some of the usual Dahl books. Some are pretty short and some are longer, with a total of seven stories. There is even a story of how Dahl got started writing. During my reading of this book, I picked up and read and small book on Dahl's life. Nice to get a big picture view of his life along with how he got his start writing. It's hard to pick one story that I liked best. Could be the story of the pick pocketer, the true story of the buried treasure, or that wonderful story of Henry Sugar. There was one story I didn't much care for due to the subject matter - the story of the swan. But that was just issues I have (touchy w/anything w/animals).<br /><br />Overall, glad I read this one to get a different take on Dahl's writing.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16772747805309963503" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1907500232" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1907500232" />
    <a title="Mariah Roze" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/22371819-mariah-roze"><img alt="Mariah Roze" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1496763524p2/22371819.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1907500232?book_show_action=true">Mar 03, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mariah Roze" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mariah Roze" href="/user/show/22371819-mariah-roze">Mariah Roze</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9781101652954" href="/book/show/16668928-the-wonderful-story-of-henry-sugar-and-six-more">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Mariah Roze by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/5903843-matt">Matt</a>
  </div>


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1907500232" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15251863532253242198">This book is made up of multiple short stories by Roald Dahl.<br/>- "The Boy Who Talked With Animals - in which a stranded sea turtle and a small boy have more in common than meets the eye.<br/>- The Hitchhiker - proves that in a pinch a professional pickpocket can be the perfect pal.<br/>- The Mildenhall Treasure - a true tale of fortune found and an opportunity lost.<br/>- The Wonderful Story of Henry Sugar - in which a modern-day Robin Hood brings joy to the hearts of orphans - and fear to the souls of casino ow</span>
  <span id="freeText15251863532253242198" style="display:none">This book is made up of multiple short stories by Roald Dahl.<br />- "The Boy Who Talked With Animals - in which a stranded sea turtle and a small boy have more in common than meets the eye.<br />- The Hitchhiker - proves that in a pinch a professional pickpocket can be the perfect pal.<br />- The Mildenhall Treasure - a true tale of fortune found and an opportunity lost.<br />- The Wonderful Story of Henry Sugar - in which a modern-day Robin Hood brings joy to the hearts of orphans - and fear to the souls of casino owners around the world."<br /><br />I did not enjoy The Boy Who Talked With Animals. I thought it was very slow, random and not entertaining. It took me a long time to get through this short story.<br /><br />The Hitchhiker was very entertaining and actually scary. There was some violence that was very unexpected in this story and the whole story definitely kept me on my toes.<br /><br />The Midenhall Treasure was a true story about treasure that was found and Roald Dahl got the opportunity to write about it for a magazine. It was interesting to read about all the laws of finding treasure in that country.<br /><br />The Wonderful Story of Henry Sugar did not have an interesting beginning to it's story. Henry read about Imhrat Khan, an Indian man with an amazing special talent. As Henry learns more about Khan he discovers that Khan's special powers is being able to see the world around him without using his eyes. Khan is able to do this because of training with a yogi. This story motivates Henry to learn how to do the same skill, so he can become a great gambler and be able to read cards. After this part is when I started to enjoy Henry Sugar's story more. Henry became a wealthy man from gambling, so he wanted to do something great with the money, so he opens many orphanages.<br /><br />The ending of the book is Dahl talking about his childhood and growing up experience. As much as I enjoyed reading about it, I was disappointed because it was so similar to the book Boy: Tales of Childhood by Roald Dahl. There was a ton of overlapping stories and there were stories that was in this book but not his autobiography. That bugged me. It should have been in his autobiography if he wanted to share it. It was a weird ending to the whole book, having it be an autobiography of random stories of his childhood. <br /><br />This was not one of my favorite Roald Dahl books, but I am glad that I read it and experienced it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15251863532253242198" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1326512658" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1326512658" />
    <a title="Rachel" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30786235-rachel"><img alt="Rachel" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1518931036p2/30786235.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1326512658?book_show_action=true">Jul 05, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rachel" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rachel" href="/user/show/30786235-rachel">Rachel</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780140057737" href="/book/show/24947.The_Wonderful_Story_of_Henry_Sugar_and_Six_More">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30786235-rachel?shelf=2015">2015</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1326512658" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15314331736792163811">Jumping back into Roald Dahl literature has been one of the best experiences in terms of reading this year.<br/><br/>I never considered that I would enjoy short stories so much. Stories that you start and finish before going to bed. Such a refreshing feeling. As a lover of Roald Dahl's stories in childhood, his writing style is one of the most easy to read and grabs-you-by-the-writing-and-plot-and-never-lets-you-go. This was such a great read and overall, my rating was based on my enjoyment.<br/><br/>Ratings for ea</span>
  <span id="freeText15314331736792163811" style="display:none">Jumping back into Roald Dahl literature has been one of the best experiences in terms of reading this year.<br /><br />I never considered that I would enjoy short stories so much. Stories that you start and finish before going to bed. Such a refreshing feeling. As a lover of Roald Dahl's stories in childhood, his writing style is one of the most easy to read and grabs-you-by-the-writing-and-plot-and-never-lets-you-go. This was such a great read and overall, my rating was based on my enjoyment.<br /><br />Ratings for each short story:<br />The Boy Who Talked with Animals: 2/5<br />The Hitch-hiker: 4/5 <br />Mildenhall Treasure: 4.5/5<br />The Swan: 2/5<br />The Wonderful Story of Henry Sugar: 5 BRILLIANT STARS/5<br />Lucky Break: 4/5 (3.5)<br />A Piece of Cake: 4/5 (3.5)<br /><br />The Boy Who Talked with Animals, I found it to be kind of pointless. The title is the story. (spoilers) Basically a boy begs a fisherman not to sell the enormous turtle so the fisherman lets the turtle go. Next day parents say their boy is missing and police are searching for him. Natives who were fishing tell police they see a boy riding a turtle into the horizon. They see the boy but he gets on turtle and rides off into the sunset. <br /><br />The Hitch-hiker was damn hilarious. This hitch-hiker with a career he won't speak off, has the most interesting banter with the main character and the story was absolutely genius. <br /><br />Mildenhall Treasure was amazing to believe that Roald Dahl had written this story of someone's recount of finding treasures that is now in the British Museum. Roald Dahl had written this story with the pure motive of telling the true story of how these treasures were found after seeing an article in the newspapers. <br /><br />The Swan, for a birdlover, was like being stabbed in the throat. A twisted story with a twisted moral.<br /><br />THE WONDERFUL STORY OF HENRY SUGAR WAS ONE OF THE MOST BEAUTIFUL STORIES I HAVE EVER READ THAT IS ALL. READ IT NOW. THANKS.<br /><br />Lucky Break went into details on some parts Dahl has written about in Boy: Tales of Childhood and Going Solo. I enjoyed seeing his perspective/role in history like World War II and the Japanese bombing of Pearl Harbour. <br /><br />A Piece of Cake, though the lower rating, was quite a good story. A story he wrote not with the intention of it being a story, was one of humour and a life threatening situation. <br /><br />All in all, a great compilation of stories and I recommend it to people who love Roald Dahl or short stories :)</span>
  <a data-text-id="15314331736792163811" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

Was poking through the others and found this gem, from Lucky Break:<br/><br/>"Here are some of the qualities you should possess or should try to acquire if you wish to be fiction writer:<br/><br/>1. You should have a lively imagination.<br/>2. You should be able to write well. By that I mean you should be able to make a scene come alive in the reader's mind. Not everybody has this ability.   <span id="freeText11886069407478341965" style="display:none">Re-read the main story but I read all of them as a kid. Was poking through the others and found this gem, from Lucky Break:<br /><br />"Here are some of the qualities you should possess or should try to acquire if you wish to be fiction writer:<br /><br />1. You should have a lively imagination.<br />2. You should be able to write well. By that I mean you should be able to make a scene come alive in the reader's mind. Not everybody has this ability. It is a gift, and you either have it or you don't.<br />3. You must have stamina. In other words, you must be able to stick to what you are doing and never give up, for hour after hour, day after day, week after week and month after month.<br />4. You must be a perfectionist. That means you must never be satisfied with what you have written until you have rewritten it again, making it as good as you possibly can.<br />5. You must have strong self-discipline. You are working alone. No one is employing you. No one is around to fire you if you don't turn up for work, or tick you off if you start slacking.<br />6. It helps a lot if you have a keen sense of humor. This is not essential when writing for grown-ups, but for children, it's vital.<br />7. You must have a degree of humility. The writer who thinks his work is marvelous is heading for trouble."</span>

<div id="review_2511676771" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2511676771" />
    <a title="Dominick" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5913578-dominick"><img alt="Dominick" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1443184611p2/5913578.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2511676771?book_show_action=true">Sep 08, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dominick" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dominick" href="/user/show/5913578-dominick">Dominick</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780140328745" href="/book/show/386245.The_Wonderful_Story_of_Henry_Sugar">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5913578-dominick?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5913578-dominick?shelf=short-stories">short-stories</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2511676771" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13970124894037181156">Odd collection. Though clearly marketed as a book for young readers, if not children per se (it says 12 and up), this does not really seem like a kids' book to me. While none of the stories include content that would be inappropriate for young readers (by many people's estimation, anyway), none of it really seems aimed at young readers, particularly. Indeed, some of the pieces--e.g. Dahl's war memoir, or his somewhat fictionalized account of the discovery of a Roman treasure hoard--were clearly </span>
  <span id="freeText13970124894037181156" style="display:none">Odd collection. Though clearly marketed as a book for young readers, if not children per se (it says 12 and up), this does not really seem like a kids' book to me. While none of the stories include content that would be inappropriate for young readers (by many people's estimation, anyway), none of it really seems aimed at young readers, particularly. Indeed, some of the pieces--e.g. Dahl's war memoir, or his somewhat fictionalized account of the discovery of a Roman treasure hoard--were clearly NOT written with children specifically in mind. Even the stories with important child characters--"The Boy Who Talked to Animals" and "The Swan" (both intriguing fables)--do not read like stories for kids. The title story is long, involves multiply embedded narrative levels, and has meta elements--again, nothing a younger reader <i>couldn't</i> handle, but also not elements that signal an intent to appeal to children, either. On the other hand, Dahl's memoir about his childhood and how he became a writer often explains and defines things one would assume most adults know, so does seem aimed at younger readers. Anyway, the result is a somewhat puzzling mix. Four of the stories are pure fiction, one is a narrativized account of fact, and two are straight-up autobiographical pieces. It feels more like Dahl had a few pieces lying around that hadn't been collected, and which he decided to combine, than it does like a coherent collection.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13970124894037181156" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer16869170698316787895">"In his short story “The Wonderful Story of Henry Sugar,” Roald Dahl develops the theme of generosity as virtuous and greed as meaningless. The protagonist, Henry Sugar, is a wealthy and lazy playboy who one day at a party reads an account written by a Dr. John Cartwright about Imhrat Khan, a man in India who could see without his eyes. Reading the account of Imhrat’s training to gain this ability, Henry Sugar decides to practice the same techniques in order to be able to see through cards at ca</span>
  <span id="freeText16869170698316787895" style="display:none">"In his short story “The Wonderful Story of Henry Sugar,” Roald Dahl develops the theme of generosity as virtuous and greed as meaningless. The protagonist, Henry Sugar, is a wealthy and lazy playboy who one day at a party reads an account written by a Dr. John Cartwright about Imhrat Khan, a man in India who could see without his eyes. Reading the account of Imhrat’s training to gain this ability, Henry Sugar decides to practice the same techniques in order to be able to see through cards at casinos. After training for three years, he wins thousands of pounds at a casino in one night, but finds that his perspective has changed. Finding meaning only in giving away his earnings, he continues to go to casinos and uses his earnings to establish twenty orphanages throughout the world."</span>

  <span id="freeText4099543625430715377" style="display:none">I was utterly, completely bowled over by this book of short stories by Roald Dahl. Never in a million years did I expect the person who entertained me throughout childhood to evoke an entirely different range of emotions in adulthood.<br /><br />The book contained 7 stories and all 7 of them broke my heart in a million pieces. The most poignant story for me was <i>"The Swan"</i> and I recommend that everybody and their dog should read it. The main story, <i>“The Wonderful Story of Henry Sugar”</i> was equally engrossing and thought-provoking.<br /><br />What made me completely fall in love with the book was the author's memoirs and his tips on how to become a fiction writer and how he got his start in the writing world. Of course, I can't forget to mention, the book also included the very first piece he had written describing his RAF days during WWII.<br /><br />Roald Dahl is a certifiable chameleon in terms of writing and I will be looking into his other books for adults as soon as possible</span>

  <span id="freeText11439721229263007602" style="display:none">Roald Dahl is a gift to children &amp; adults alike. These stories lit up my life! They brought me joy, immersed me, &amp; one kind of horrified me... But they were incredibly entertaining. Out of all the stories, I loved “Piece of Cake” the most. Mostly because I really enjoyed knowing it was his first story he ever wrote &amp; he didn’t even mean to write it that well 😂 His words on how he even became a writer BLEW MY MIND! What a lucky break indeed! Dahl has stolen my heart with this book &amp; I now need to read everything he’s ever written. He is funny, witty, &amp; incredibly well-versed in literature. He expands so well on characters &amp; used intense imagery &amp; words I’ve never heard before! What an expansive vocabulary he has. What an amazing book! PLEASE read these short stories! I was so wonderfully entertained by them &amp; would recommend this to absolutely everyone. </span>

<div id="review_3055427429" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3055427429" />
    <a title="Jamie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/53587416-jamie"><img alt="Jamie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1571965612p2/53587416.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3055427429?book_show_action=true">Dec 17, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jamie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jamie" href="/user/show/53587416-jamie">Jamie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3055427429" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5598214194109046412">The title story, The Wonderful Story of Henry Sugar, is really a treasure. A wonderful and inspiring story for both adults and children. I also quite enjoyed The Boy Who Talked with Animals and The Mildenhall Treasure, the latter which is based on a fascinating real-life story of buried treasure. In typical Dahl fashion, many of the stories have some dark elements, deaths, beatings, etc. The Swan in particular is quite dark and sadistic.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_52458073" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/52458073" />
    <a title="PurplyCookie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2214498-purplycookie"><img alt="PurplyCookie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1415491715p2/2214498.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/52458073?book_show_action=true">Apr 12, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="PurplyCookie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="PurplyCookie" href="/user/show/2214498-purplycookie">PurplyCookie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780141304700" href="/book/show/385246.The_Wonderful_Story_of_Henry_Sugar_and_Six_More">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2214498-purplycookie?shelf=short-stories">short-stories</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2214498-purplycookie?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer52458073" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7890273225460139236">If you could see with your eyes closed, how would you use your power? That’s what Henry has to decide in one of the seven stories in this extraordinary collection. <br/><br/><b>"The Boy Who Talked With Animals"</b> >> Is about a young tourist boy at a beach resort who seeks to free a giant sea turtle which has been captured by the hotel management. This sounds like a children's story, but the characterization and the setting are quite adult.<br/><br/><b>"The Hitchhiker"</b> >> Is an amusing tale about a British hitchhiker who re</span>
  <span id="freeText7890273225460139236" style="display:none">If you could see with your eyes closed, how would you use your power? That’s what Henry has to decide in one of the seven stories in this extraordinary collection. <br /><br /><b>"The Boy Who Talked With Animals"</b> &gt;&gt; Is about a young tourist boy at a beach resort who seeks to free a giant sea turtle which has been captured by the hotel management. This sounds like a children's story, but the characterization and the setting are quite adult.<br /><br /><b>"The Hitchhiker"</b> &gt;&gt; Is an amusing tale about a British hitchhiker who reveals himself to be a "fingersmith", a master classman of the pickpocketing profession. The interplay between three different levels of British society: the journalist driver, the rough cockney passenger, and a belligerent traffic cop proves to be an entertaining read. Certainly my most favorite stories in this collection, followed closely by that of Henry Sugar. <br /><br /><b>"The Mildenhall Treasure"</b> &gt;&gt; Is an incredible story about an amazing discovery. On a cold winter morning, a farmer plowing another man's land stumbled upon the greatest cache of Roman silver ever found in Britain. Regrettably, Gordon Butcher didn't know what he had found because the silver had tarnished during its years in the ground. His boss did know what it was and took the stuff home where hid it for a few years before the authorities discovered it. The crux of the story centers on a British law that says the person who FINDS any treasure receives compensation for the full market value of the items. The Mildenhall plates, bowls, and spoons would have netted Butcher nearly a million pounds. By allowing his boss to walk off with the silver, Butcher received only one thousand pounds. In a way, this book is similar to the Mildenhall Treasure: a great find even if you have little idea of it at first glance. This is one of the only two non-fiction stories that Dahl ever wrote. <br /><br /><b>"The Swan"</b> &gt;&gt; About a precocious child named Peter Watson who runs into two local tormentors, Ernie and Raymond, while out bird watching. The two goons march Watson around at the point of a gun for no other reason than alleviating their boredom on a weekend. The final indignity occurs when Raymond and Ernie shoot a beautiful swan, tie its wings to Peter's arms, and force him to climb a tree so they can see him "fly." There is something magical and memorable about what happens next as Peter learns that he is one of those precious souls which all the bullies in the world will never triumph over.<br /><br /><b>"The Wonderful Story of Henry Sugar"</b> &gt;&gt; It's really two stories in one, about a wealthy but frivolous soul named Henry Sugar (of an affluent British family) and his discovery of an unusual book in a friend's library. The book tells the story about a man in India (Imhan Khan) who has learned to see through objects without the use of his eyes. Sugar gets the sudden inspiration to attain this ability and soon discovers that he is a natural at it, one of the rare people with the amazing gift to learn this art in just a few years. Henry's motivations are highly suspect at first: he wishes to use this newfound talent to cheat at the casino, thereby earning himself a fortune. But something rather odd occurs during his training process when Sugar soon discovers that he has little interest in accumulating money for selfish ends. Dahl writes the story in such a way that the reader becomes convinced Henry Sugar was a real, breathing person. <br /><br /><br />In addition to these imaginative and magical tales, this book also contains the true story of how Roald Dahl became a writer, as well as a copy of the very first nonfiction story he wrote for The Saturday Evening Post:<br /><br /><b>"Lucky Break: How I Became A Writer"</b> &gt;&gt; This story is really a short autobiography of the writer from his early school days through his war experiences. The sections outlining his years at one of England's public schools should be read by anyone who thinks American places of learning are terrible. English public schools, Dahl writes, are actually very private academies devoted to the total education of their pupils. During the writer's childhood, this meant harsh, rigid discipline of a type usually seen in the military. The brutality exhibited by teachers and elder classmates at the school is shocking: the older students routinely whipped younger pupils with switches, an activity mirrored by the teachers whenever students misbehaved. There are great, tension filled descriptions of the beatings endured by Dahl at the hands of these tormentors. I would've loved to have had Mrs. O'Connor as a professor! She was indeed a fountain of information for the greatest of English literature. <br /><br /><b>"A Piece of Cake: First Story-1942"</b> &gt;&gt; This was Dahl's first published story, which appears to be based on his wartime experiences without necessarily being 100% accurate in its minor details. For an enthusiastic Dahl fan like myself, getting a glimpse of the man behind the curtain is exciting, and getting to know more about Dahl is a real treat.<br /><br /><br /><u>Book Details: </u><br /><br /><u>Title</u> The Wonderful Story of Henry Sugar and Six More<br /><u>Author</u> Roald Dahl<br /><u>Reviewed By</u> Purplycookie</span>
  <a data-text-id="7890273225460139236" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/421719410?book_show_action=true">Sep 25, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dolly" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dolly" href="/user/show/1019021-dolly">Dolly</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">parents reading with their children</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1019021-dolly?shelf=caribbean">caribbean</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1019021-dolly?shelf=aviation">aviation</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1019021-dolly?shelf=ocean-seashore">ocean-seashore</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1019021-dolly?shelf=egyptian">egyptian</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1019021-dolly?shelf=english">english</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1019021-dolly?shelf=washington-dc">washington-dc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1019021-dolly?shelf=2014">2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1019021-dolly?shelf=thailand">thailand</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1019021-dolly?shelf=education-school">education-school</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1019021-dolly?shelf=switzerland">switzerland</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer421719410" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3614815060993936789">This is a wonderful collection of short stories, a collection of tales that could only come from the inimitable <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4273.Roald_Dahl' title='Roald Dahl' rel='nofollow noopener'>Roald Dahl</a>. We read this book slowly, at most one story each night, and savored each one. <br/><br/>That is, until we got to the middle of the book. For some reason, once we came to the title tale, we stopped. cold. As in, couldn't seem to pick the book up again for more than a year. I tried, believe me. I put the book on hold, borrowed it, and even tried to start the story, but we just never go</span>
  <span id="freeText3614815060993936789" style="display:none">This is a wonderful collection of short stories, a collection of tales that could only come from the inimitable <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4273.Roald_Dahl" title="Roald Dahl" rel="nofollow noopener">Roald Dahl</a>. We read this book slowly, at most one story each night, and savored each one. <br /><br />That is, until we got to the middle of the book. For some reason, once we came to the title tale, we stopped. cold. As in, couldn't seem to pick the book up again for more than a year. I tried, believe me. I put the book on hold, borrowed it, and even tried to start the story, but we just never got into it and the book would sit until it was time to return it. <br /><br />Finally, as I realized the book was coming due yet again, I was determined to finish it one way or another. And I have to admit that it was a rather engaging tale, once we got into it. The true story of how he first got into writing was fascinating to me, but our girls quickly lost interest. And I didn't even try to read them his first published short story, <i>A Piece of Cake</i>. I thought it was very good, but I'm not sure they are ready for that kind of tale. <br /><br />I loved that the third story featured a town in England that I have become quite familiar with - it's right outside of an airbase (aptly named RAF Mildenhall) that I've visited countless times and have stayed at for more than six months altogether. One of my favorite things to do when we go to England is to walk the three miles or so into town, get some fish and chips at the local shop and then walk to the River Ouse and enjoy the sunshine (for some reason, it always seems to defy the stereotypical rainy weather when I go there.) I feed the ducks and watch the numerous people enjoying the walking trails, benches and playing fields. <br /><br />Overall, I thought that this was a terrific book of short stories and I'm sorry that we took so long to finish it. I don't even know why this happened, really, although I think that the title story does start a bit slowly. Still, we have really enjoyed reading <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4273.Roald_Dahl" title="Roald Dahl" rel="nofollow noopener">Roald Dahl</a>'s books and we will be sure to look for more of them at our local library.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3614815060993936789" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_207094330" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Maria" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6105815-maria"><img alt="Maria" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/207094330?book_show_action=true">Sep 10, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maria" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maria" href="/user/show/6105815-maria">Maria</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer207094330" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9745560149123061304">Remembering the joy of reading Road Dahl as a child, I felt very excited when I received ‘The Wonderful Story of Henry Sugar, And Six More’ as a birthday present. I read this book eagerly and was not disappointed. With seven short stories to capture the reader; including fiction and non-fiction, Roald Dahl once again writes with imagination, wit and intelligence. His use of description throughout these stories is spot on, enabling the reader to conjure some fantastic images. From a boy who can t</span>
  <span id="freeText9745560149123061304" style="display:none">Remembering the joy of reading Road Dahl as a child, I felt very excited when I received ‘The Wonderful Story of Henry Sugar, And Six More’ as a birthday present. I read this book eagerly and was not disappointed. With seven short stories to capture the reader; including fiction and non-fiction, Roald Dahl once again writes with imagination, wit and intelligence. His use of description throughout these stories is spot on, enabling the reader to conjure some fantastic images. From a boy who can talk to animals to a man who sees with his eyes closed, Dahl hooked me from the beginning with originality and surprise. <br /><br />Whilst mystery and humour most definitely exist, these stories do not stop here. Dahl’s clever way of writing makes the reader think beneath the surface and learn some valuable lessons throughout. ‘The Boy Who Talked with Animals’ for example, made me stop and think about kindness, greed and the importance of being true to what we believe in. <br /><br />I feel that with careful choosing, this book would be most enjoyable and beneficial to children in Year 6. There is one story in particular titled ‘The Swan’ which I feel is aimed towards an older age group. Whilst it is clearly written well, it is very dark and even I, as an adult found it quite disturbing and sad. <br /><br />I thoroughly enjoyed this book and appreciated the mix between fiction and non-fiction. ‘Lucky Break’ and ‘A Piece of Cake’ allowed me to learn a little more about the great writer himself and once again appreciate his talent. <br /><br />To be a good fiction writer (as Roald Dahl explains) “you should have imagination…make a scene come alive, and a keen sense of humour.” Throughout this book he most definitely ticks these boxes, compiling an interesting, humorous and enjoyable read. As always, a big thumbs up Roald Dahl!</span>
  <a data-text-id="9745560149123061304" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_101305138" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/101305138" />
    <a title="Julie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1054264-julie"><img alt="Julie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1314411439p2/1054264.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/101305138?book_show_action=true">May 04, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Julie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Julie" href="/user/show/1054264-julie">Julie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer101305138" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8936607436001689625">I was really torn about giving this 3 or 4 stars. I loved two of the stories especially, but the others were a little more average. The whole collection really wasn't what I expected, after my many years of reading Dahl's books. Unlike his children's books (which is where this book is shelved), there are very few children involved and while the stories do have some whimsical elements they aren't nearly as fantastical as his books. I was trying to decide the whole time if I would have liked the s</span>
  <span id="freeText8936607436001689625" style="display:none">I was really torn about giving this 3 or 4 stars. I loved two of the stories especially, but the others were a little more average. The whole collection really wasn't what I expected, after my many years of reading Dahl's books. Unlike his children's books (which is where this book is shelved), there are very few children involved and while the stories do have some whimsical elements they aren't nearly as fantastical as his books. I was trying to decide the whole time if I would have liked the stories if I'd read them when I was younger. I like to think I still would have enjoyed them, but I don't think it would have been a repeat for me. <br /><br />Strangely enough, I liked two of the three nonfiction stories the best--"The Mildenhall Treasure" and "Lucky Break." "Lucky Break" was all about his path to becoming a writer and it was quite fascinating. The rest of the book was worth reading to get to that one at the end. <br /><br />On the downside, "The Swan" kind of made me feel ill because what happens in it is so awful (it's about two bullies tormenting a little nerdling). </span>
  <a data-text-id="8936607436001689625" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Andy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Andy" href="/user/show/1251066-andy">Andy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780140057737" href="/book/show/24947.The_Wonderful_Story_of_Henry_Sugar_and_Six_More">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1251066-andy?shelf=2011">2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1251066-andy?shelf=short-stories">short-stories</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer192749940" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13953278287295713721">This is another book which has sat on various shelves for many months now before finally being completed. The short stories (7 of them) are mainly directed at an older age group though touch on similar themes to his younger work. My copy has a different cover which doesn't appear here.<br/><br/>I've read 'The Hitch-hiker' before and enjoyed it, found 'The Swan' quite dark and disturbing (taking the bullying of his younger books to more dangerous regions). 'Henry Sugar' though felt a little disappointing. </span>
  <span id="freeText13953278287295713721" style="display:none">This is another book which has sat on various shelves for many months now before finally being completed. The short stories (7 of them) are mainly directed at an older age group though touch on similar themes to his younger work. My copy has a different cover which doesn't appear here.<br /><br />I've read 'The Hitch-hiker' before and enjoyed it, found 'The Swan' quite dark and disturbing (taking the bullying of his younger books to more dangerous regions). 'Henry Sugar' though felt a little disappointing. A story, within a story, within a story which meanders through yoga and mysticism, gambling and self discovery towards a vague morale (perhaps, I'm not quite sure). I did quite like Lucky Break, detailing briefly how he became a writer (like a condensed version of Boy and Going Solo) and the accompanying 'A piece of cake', his first written and published story. 'The Mildenhall Treasure' just didn't interest me though, feeling unsatisfying.<br /><br />Not bad, I just prefer his children's books.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13953278287295713721" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_3124950571" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3124950571" />
    <a title="Mike" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27986103-mike"><img alt="Mike" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1441940772p2/27986103.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3124950571?book_show_action=true">Jan 05, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mike" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mike" href="/user/show/27986103-mike">Mike</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3124950571" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8276895086782116152">A bit of a mixed bag. All of the stories are very readable, but not all of them go anywhere - some of them end quite oddly. <i>Henry Sugar</i> comes to a certain point, the author intrudes thoroughly, and then takes the story off in an almost apologetic way that seems at odds with what's gone before. Similarly in <i>The Swan</i>, one of Dahl's typically grim and nasty pieces, we have an ending that connects in no way with what is an otherwise realistic story. <br/>And there's that odd amoral feeling about some of </span>
  <span id="freeText8276895086782116152" style="display:none">A bit of a mixed bag. All of the stories are very readable, but not all of them go anywhere - some of them end quite oddly. <i>Henry Sugar</i> comes to a certain point, the author intrudes thoroughly, and then takes the story off in an almost apologetic way that seems at odds with what's gone before. Similarly in <i>The Swan</i>, one of Dahl's typically grim and nasty pieces, we have an ending that connects in no way with what is an otherwise realistic story. <br />And there's that odd amoral feeling about some of them that you find in some of his other longer stories, such as <i>Danny, the Champion of the World</i>. Here, in <i>The Hitch-hiker</i>, Dahl seems to delight in the fact that the law is made a fool of. I often wonder what message children take out of his books...<br />The two non-fiction pieces, The <i>Mildenhall Treasure</i>, and <i>Lucky Break</i> are interesting to read, but feel as though they've been well and truly dramatised. And is Dahl serious in telling us that he wrote a piece that was worthy of publication when he'd never written anything like that before?</span>
  <a data-text-id="8276895086782116152" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2230063279" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2230063279" />
    <a title="Cathleen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/71311706-cathleen"><img alt="Cathleen" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2230063279?book_show_action=true">Dec 28, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cathleen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cathleen" href="/user/show/71311706-cathleen">Cathleen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2230063279" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16529133428371698495">I recently read The Wonderful Story of Henry Sugar and Six More by Roald Dahl, which tells short stories on a greedy man who changes his lifestyle. In my opinion, Roald Dahl is one of the best authors since he can turn fantasy and unbelievable novels into novels that seem realistic, but still unbelievable. Because of this sense, reading this book has been a wondrous adventure that I couldn't have gotten from other authors. The story of Henry Sugar reminded me a lot of a movie made in 2016 called</span>
  <span id="freeText16529133428371698495" style="display:none">I recently read The Wonderful Story of Henry Sugar and Six More by Roald Dahl, which tells short stories on a greedy man who changes his lifestyle. In my opinion, Roald Dahl is one of the best authors since he can turn fantasy and unbelievable novels into novels that seem realistic, but still unbelievable. Because of this sense, reading this book has been a wondrous adventure that I couldn't have gotten from other authors. The story of Henry Sugar reminded me a lot of a movie made in 2016 called, "Doctor Strange". The journeys between both books are very similar, although every plot follows the Hero's Journey, as mentioned in A Hero of A Thousand Faces by Joseph Campbell. Both of these characters follow a yoga path, which is the style of magic and concentrating the inner and outer mind. These characters intentionally try to use the power for personal gain but eventually uses it to help others. One moment in this book that really ties the whole plot together was Henry Sugar's moment of realization. Usually, in fantasy books, you rarely find anything that has to do with thinking or concentrating. Henry Sugar had a thought, after 3 years of the path of yoga, to help others such as an orphanage. This seemed pretty realistic, like how Steve Jobs created the iPod because he thought of his daughter and her cassette. Overall, I enjoyed this book with its realistically not realistic theme. </span>
  <a data-text-id="16529133428371698495" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('L0ML9TxDuAuvlllsE3gxK0Gdft/L3SY1gSUWlS4p9iBy7QiyIQH8iPMp7C8vFGIfw65yIvlL2HQDKVevmi6CIQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('+xNntsUpAyxYYeWaMlMPIEQD5YdG6q0w+9hjIWpBx3OmvWTx2GtHrwTeUNkOP1wUxjDpenR8U3F51CIb3kazcg==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer5559768432332439291">Roald Dahl was a British novelist, short story writer and screenwriter of Norwegian descent, who rose to prominence in the 1940's with works for both children and adults, and became one of the world's bestselling authors.<br/><br/>Dahl's first published work, inspired by a meeting with C. S. Forester, was <i>Shot Down Over Libya</i>. Today the story is published as <i>A Piece of Cake</i>. The story, about his wartime adv</span>
  <span id="freeText5559768432332439291" style="display:none">Roald Dahl was a British novelist, short story writer and screenwriter of Norwegian descent, who rose to prominence in the 1940's with works for both children and adults, and became one of the world's bestselling authors.<br /><br />Dahl's first published work, inspired by a meeting with C. S. Forester, was <i>Shot Down Over Libya</i>. Today the story is published as <i>A Piece of Cake</i>. The story, about his wartime adventures, was bought by the Saturday Evening Post for $900, and propelled him into a career as a writer. Its title was inspired by a highly inaccurate and sensationalized article about the crash that blinded him, which claimed he had been shot down instead of simply having to land because of low fuel.<br /><br />His first children's book was <i>The Gremlins</i>, about mischievous little creatures that were part of RAF folklore. The book was commissioned by Walt Disney for a film that was never made, and published in 1943. Dahl went on to create some of the best-loved children's stories of the 20th century, such as <i>Charlie and the Chocolate Factory</i>, <i>Matilda</i> and <i>James and the Giant Peach</i>.<br /><br />He also had a successful parallel career as the writer of macabre adult short stories, usually with a dark sense of humour and a surprise ending. Many were originally written for American magazines such as <i>Ladies Home Journal</i>, <i>Harper's</i>, <i>Playboy</i> and <i>The New Yorker</i>, then subsequently collected by Dahl into anthologies, gaining world-wide acclaim. Dahl wrote more than 60 short stories and they have appeared in numerous collections, some only being published in book form after his death. His stories also brought him three Edgar Awards: in 1954, for the collection <i>Someone Like You</i>; in 1959, for the story "The Landlady"; and in 1980, for the episode of <i>Tales of the Unexpected</i> based on "Skin".</span>
  <a data-text-id="5559768432332439291" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      <div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/work/quotes/3159194-the-wonderful-story-of-henry-sugar-and-six-more">Quotes from The Wonderful Sto...</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">

            <span class="readable">&ldquo;Some people when they have taken too much and have been driven beyond the point of endurance, simply crumble and give up. There are others, though they are not many, who will for some reason always be unconquerable. You meet them in time of war and also in time of peace. They have an indomitable spirit and nothing, neither pain nor torture nor threat of death, will cause them to give up.&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/900439-some-people-when-they-have-taken-too-much-and-have">44 likes</a>
            </nobr>
            <div class="clear"></div>
          </div>
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;And it was then I began to realize for the first time that there are two distinct sides to a writer of fiction. First, there is the side he displays to the public, that of an ordinary person like anyone else, a person who does ordinary things and speaks ordinary language. Second, there is the secret side, which comes out in him only after he has closed the door of his workroom and is completely alone. It is then that he slips into another world altogether, a world where his imagination takes over and he finds himself actually living in the places he is writing about at that moment. I myself, if you want to know, fall into a kind of trance, and everything around me disappears. I see only the point of my pencil moving over the paper, and quite often two hours go by as though they were a couple of seconds.&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
